Rulings of Hajr for Minors, Insane, and Slaves
States rulings on hajr for minor, insane, and slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on the validity of transactions and confessions of minors, insane persons, and slaves according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Minors and the severely insane have no legal capacity; a slave's confession binds himself but not his master.

This lesson covers the basic principles of legal interdiction (hajr) according to the Hanafi school. The text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains that minors and the insane lack capacity, so their statements and actions are generally invalid. A slave has limited capacity: his confession is valid only regarding his own person. Additionally, persons under interdiction are liable for any damage they cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of persons under hajr
The text mentions minors, insane persons, and slaves as subjects of hajr. Note the legal definition of each: minor (not reached puberty), insane (intellect disordered), slave (owned by another).
The severely insane (maghlub) is distinguished from the imbecile (ma'tuh).
2
Analyze liability for damage
Any interdicted person who causes damage to life or property must compensate, because actions of the limbs do not require intent for liability.
The sleeping person example shows that even without intent, liability exists.
3
Evaluate the rule on confession
The confession of a minor or insane person is never effective in any matter. The confession of a slave is effective only regarding himself, not against his master.
The hadith 'raf' al-qalam' is cited as proof for minors and insane.
4
Understand the distinction between severely insane and imbecile
The severely insane (maghlub) has absolutely no valid actions. The imbecile (ma'tuh) has some capacity and is treated like a minor or slave in some rulings.
This distinction resolves a grammatical issue in the text about pronoun reference.
5
Connect the hadith proof
The hadith 'The pen is lifted from three' provides the basis for lifting accountability and legal effect from minors and insane persons.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجر وحكمه
يجيزه الولي أو يفسخه، وإن أتلفوا شيئا ضمنوا، ولا ينفذ إقرار الصبي والمجنون، إن شاء أي العقد أي هؤلاء من نفس أو مال وينفذ إقرار العبد في حقه لا في حق سيّده، ويصح إتيان ضمير الجمع، لكن لا يصح الحكم بتوقف العقد، وخيار الولي بالإجازة أو الفسخ مطلقا فإن تصرف المجنون المغلوب لا يصح أصلا، وإن كان راجعا إلى الصغير والرقيق يصح الحكم بالتوقف والخيار لكن ليس إتيان ضمير الجمع على محله، بل كان ينبغي أن يقول: "منهما"، وإن كان راجعا إلى الصغير والرقيق والمعتوه صح الحكم وصح إتيان الضمير، لكن يلزم أن لا يكون بعض المرجع مذكورا. والجواب عنه أنا نختار الشق الثالث ونقول: المجنون على نوعين: مجنون مغلوب وهو الذي اختلط عقله بحيث يمنع جريان الأفعال والأقوال على نهج العقل إلا نادرا وتصرفه لا يصح، ومجنون غير مغلوب وهو الذي يختلط كلامه فيشبه مرة كلام العقلاء ومرة لا وهو المعتوه، ولما ذكر المجنون المغلوب فهم منه غير المغلوب الذي بمنزلة الصبي والعبد فيكون مرجع الضمير مذكورا ضمنا فلا إشكال، ويمكن الجواب باختيار الشق الثاني ونقول: أتي بضمير الجمع وأراد به التثنية وهو شائع كذا قيل هذا ملخص ما في التكملة و"ملا مسكين"، وفيه كلام طويل ليس هذا موضعه.
ضمنوا؛ لما وإن أتلفوا شيئا إلخ: هذا تفريع على قوله: "لا" فعلا": أي إن أتلف هؤلاء المحجورون شيئا من نفس أو مال أنه لا حجر في أفعال الجوارح؛ لأن اعتبار الفعل لا يتوقف على القصد، فإن النائم إذا انقلب على مال إنسان وأتلفه، ضمن، وإن عدم القصد، لكنه لا يخاطب بالأداء إلا عند القدرة كالمعسر لا يطالب بالدين إلا إذا أيسر، وكالنائم لا يطالب بالأداء إلا إذا استيقظ، وقد اختلفوا في أن الضمان يجب للحال، أو بعد البلوغ والعتق، وظاهر هذا التعليل أنه لا يجب إلا بعد البلوغ والعتق وقد نقل في "التكملة" [١٥٧/٨]: عن "الحدادي"، و"العناية" كلاما يدل على أنه يجب في الحال، ومن أراد التفصيل فلينظر في "التكملة" و"الفتح".
ولا ينفذ إقرار إلخ أي لا ينفذ إقرار الصبي والمجنون مطلقا لا بمال ولا بحد من الحدود ولا بالطلاق ولا بالعتاق؛ لقوله عليه: رفع القلم عن ثلاثة عن الصبي حتى يحتلم، وعن المجنون حتى يفيق، وظاهره يقتضي أن لا يتعلق بأقوالهما حكم [ رمز الحقائق: ۳۱۳/۲]؛ ولأن اعتبار الأقوال في الشرع منوطة بالأهلية، وهي معدومة فيهما، حتى لو تعلق بإقرارهما حكم شرعي كالحد لا يعتبر أيضا إلا من حيث إنه إتلاف، فيجب الضمان، لا يقال: هذا الحكم أي عدم نفوذ إقرارهما علم من قوله: "قولا"؛ لأنا نقول: إنما علم منه بطريق التضمين، والتصريح أبلغ. فكذا ذكره تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥٧/٨]
وينفذ إقرار إلخ: أي ينفذ إقرار العبد في حقه لقيام الأهلية لا في حق سيده رعاية لجانبه؛ لأن نفاذه لا يعرى عن تعلق الدين برقبته وكسبه وكلاهما إتلاف ماله. (فتح)

كتاب الحجر
٢٣٤
الحجر وحكمه
فلو أقرّ بمال لزمه بعد الحرية، ولو أقر بحد أو قود، لزمه في الحال لا بسفه، على نفسه لزوال المانع أي العبد قصاص فلو أقر بمال إلخ: أي لو أقر العبد بمال لأحد لزمه المال بعد العتق لا في الحال؛ لأنه إقرار على غيره، وهو المولى، لما أنه وما في يده ملكه، وإقرار الرجل على غيره لا يقبل، فإذا أعتق زال المانع ووجب المال لوجود الأهلية. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥٧/٨، ١٠٨] لزمه في الحال أي يلزمه الحد والقود في الحال؛ لأنه يبقى على أصل الحرية في حقهما. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١۵٨/۸] فإن قيل: قال: "لا يملك العبد والمكاتب شيئا إلا الطلاق"، و"شيئا" نكرة في سياق النفي فتعم فيقتضي أن لا يملك الإقرار بالحدود والقصاص؟ قلنا: لما بقي على أصل الحرية في حقهما يكون إقراره بهما إقرار بالحرية لا بالعبدية؛ ولأن قوله تعالى: بَلِ الْإِنْسَانُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بَصِيرَةٌ (القيامة: ١٤) يقتضي أن يصح إقراره ره فينفذ، ولا يقال: إنه خص منه الإقرار بالمال؛ لأنا نقول: الإقرار بالمال ليس بإقرار على نفسه وإنما هو إقرار على غيره فلم يتناوله النص. (فتح، تكملة)
لا بسفه: أي لا يحجر على الحر العاقل البالغ بسبب سفه عند الإمام، والسفه: هو العمل بخلاف موجب الشرع واتباع الهوى ومن عادة السفيه التبذير والإسراف في النفقة والتصرفات لا لغرض أو لغرض لا يعده العقلاء من أهل الديانة غرضا مثل دفع المال إلى المغني واللعاب، وشراء الحمام للطيارة بثمن غال والغبن في التجارات من غير محمدة رمز الحقائق: ۳۱۳/۲] وأصل المسامحات في التصرفات والبر والإحسان مشروع إلا أن الإسراف حرام كالإسراف في الطعام والشراب، قال تعالى: ﴿إِذَا أَنْفَقُوا لَمْ يُسْرِفُوا وَلَمْ يَقْتُرُوا (الفرقان:٦٧)، وعندهما: يحجر السفه في تصرفات لا تصح مع الهزل كالبيع والهبة والإجارة والصدقة ولا يحجر عليه في غيرها كالطلاق والعتاق والنكاح وغيرها، وقال الشافعي: يحجر عليه في الكل لهما: أن الحجر على الصبي لاحتمال التبذير، فلأن يحجر على السفيه مع تيقن التبذير كان أحرى وبه قال مالك وأحمد وله أنه مخاطب فلا يحجر عليه كالرشيد، ولأنه لا يندفع الضرر عنه بالحجر، فإنه يقدر على إتلاف ماله بتزويج الأربع، وتطليقهن قبل الدخول وبعده في كل يوم ووقت، ولو كان في الحجر عليه دفع الضرر جاز كالمفتي الماجن والطبيب الجاهل والمكاري المفلس، لكن قدمنا أن الحجر على المفتي والطبيب والمكاري ليس بحجر اصطلاحي.
قال في "رد المحتار": وأما الحجر على المفتي الماجن وأخويه، فليس بحجر اصطلاحي، وهذا إذا بلغ عاقلا رشيدا ثم سفه، وأما إذا بلغ سفيها، فقد بين المصنف حكمه بقوله: "فإن بلغ إلخ، ثم بعد اتفاقهما على أن الحجر يكون بالسفه اختلفا في أنه هل يكون بمجرد السفه أم بقضاء القاضي؟ فعند أبي يوسف لا يصير محجورا إلا بالقضاء، ولا يصير مطلقا إلا بإطلاق القاضي، وعند محمد يحجر بدون حجر القاضي، وينطلق بترك السفه، قال في "الدر المختار" وغيره: الفتوى على قولهما، ويكون السفيه عندهما كالصغير في جميع الأحكام إلا في النكاح والطلاق والعتاق والاستيلاد والتدبير ووجوب الزكاة والحج والعبادات وزوال ولاية أبيه وجده، وفي صحة إقراره بالعقوبات، وفي الإيقاف وفي صحة وصاياه بالقرب من الثلث، فهو في هذه كالعاقل من العيني والفتح ورد المحتار وغيرها)
The chapter of interdiction and its ruling. The guardian may authorize or annul it. If they damage something, they are liable. The confession of a minor and an insane person is not executed. If he wishes, meaning the contract, meaning these persons regarding life or property. The confession of a slave is executed regarding himself, not regarding his master. The use of the plural pronoun is correct, but the ruling of suspending the contract is not correct, and the guardian has the option of authorization or annulment absolutely. Indeed, the action of the severely insane (maghlub) is not valid at all. But if it refers to the minor and the slave, the ruling of suspension and option is correct, but the use of the plural pronoun is not in its proper place; rather it should say 'from them both' (minhuma). And if it refers to the minor, the slave, and the imbecile (ma'tuh), the ruling is correct and the use of the pronoun is correct, but it would require that some referent is not mentioned. The response is that we choose the third option and say: the insane are of two types: the severely insane whose intellect is so confused that it prevents actions and words from following a rational pattern except rarely, and his actions are not valid; and the non-severely insane whose speech is mixed, sometimes resembling rational speech and sometimes not, and he is the imbecile. Since the severely insane was mentioned, the non-severely insane is understood, who is like the minor and slave, so the referent of the pronoun is implicitly mentioned, so no problem. It is also possible to choose the second option and say: the plural pronoun was used intending the dual, which is common. This is the summary of what is in al-Takmila and Mulla Miskin, but there is lengthy discussion not appropriate here. They are liable; as for 'if they damage something' etc.: this is a branch of his statement 'No' in deed: i.e., if these interdicted persons damage something regarding life or property, there is no interdiction regarding actions of the limbs, because the consideration of the action does not depend on intention. For if a sleeping person rolls onto someone's property and damages it, he is liable despite lacking intention, but he is not addressed for payment until he is able, like the insolvent debtor who is not demanded until he becomes wealthy, and like the sleeping person who is not demanded until he wakes. They differed on whether liability is immediate or after puberty and manumission. The apparent meaning of this reasoning is that it is not due until after puberty and manumission. It was narrated in al-Takmila from al-Haddad and al-Inaya that it is due immediately. Whoever wants details should look into al-Takmila and al-Fath. 'The confession of a minor and an insane person is not executed' etc.: i.e., the confession of a minor and an insane person is absolutely not executed, neither regarding property nor regarding a prescribed punishment nor regarding divorce nor regarding manumission, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'The pen is lifted from three: from the minor until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he recovers.' Its apparent meaning requires that no ruling is attached to their statements. And because the consideration of statements in the Sharia is dependent on legal capacity, which is absent in both. Even if a legal ruling like a prescribed punishment is attached to their confession, it is not considered except from the aspect that it is destruction, so liability is required. It cannot be said: this ruling, i.e., the non-execution of their confession, is known from his statement 'statement' (qawlan); because we say: it is only known from it by implication, and explicit statement is more emphatic. This is mentioned in Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. 'The confession of a slave is executed' etc.: i.e., the confession of a slave is executed regarding himself due to the existence of legal capacity, not regarding his master, out of consideration for the master's side, because its execution is not free from entailing debt on his person and his earnings, both of which are destruction of his property. (Al-Fath) Now i.e., the [PAGE_235] Chapter of Interdiction 234. The chapter of interdiction and its ruling. If he confesses to a property, it becomes binding after manumission. If he confesses to a prescribed punishment or retaliation, it becomes binding immediately. Not due to foolishness, on himself due to the removal of the barrier, i.e., the slave. Retaliation. 'If he confesses to property' etc.: i.e., if a slave confesses to a property for someone, the property becomes binding after manumission, not immediately, because it is a confession against another, i.e., the master, since what he possesses belongs to his master. The confession of a person against another is not accepted. When he is freed, the barrier is removed and the property becomes due due to the existence of legal capacity. Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. 'Immediately' i.e., the prescribed punishment and retaliation become binding immediately because he remains on the original freedom regarding them. Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. If it is said: He (the Prophet) said: 'The slave and the mukatib do not own anything except divorce,' and 'anything' is indefinite in the context of negation so it generalizes, implying that he does not own confession regarding punishments and retaliation? We reply: Since he remains on the original freedom regarding them, his confession regarding them is a confession of freedom, not of slavery. And because the statement of Allah: 'Rather, man is a witness against himself' (Qiyamah: 14) implies that his confession is valid and executed. And it cannot be said that confession regarding property is excepted from that; because we say: confession regarding property is not a confession against himself but rather against another, so the text does not cover it. (Al-Fath, Takmila) 'Not due to foolishness' (la bisafah): i.e., a free, sane, adult person is not interdicted due to foolishness according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). Foolishness (safah) is acting contrary to the requirements of the Sharia and following whims. It is the habit of the fool (safih) to waste and overspend in expenses and transactions for no purpose or for a purpose that rational people of religion do not consider a purpose, such as giving money to a singer or a player, buying pigeons for flying at an exorbitant price, and being cheated in trades without commendation. The basic principle of leniency in transactions and charity and beneficence is legislated, but extravagance is forbidden, like extravagance in food and drink. Allah said: 'When they spend, they are not extravagant and not miserly' (Al-Furqan: 67). According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the fool is interdicted in transactions that are not valid with jest, like sale, gift, lease, and charity, but he is not interdicted in others like divorce, manumission, marriage, and others. Al-Shafi'i said: He is interdicted in all. For them (the two disciples): Interdiction of a minor is due to the possibility of waste, so it is more appropriate to interdict the fool with confirmed waste. Malik and Ahmad also said this. For him (Abu Hanifa): He is legally addressed, so he is not interdicted, like the mature person. And because harm cannot be repelled from him by interdiction, for he is able to destroy his property by marrying four women and divorcing them before and after consummation every day and time. If interdiction repelled harm, it would be permissible, like the mischievous mufti, the ignorant doctor, and the bankrupt transporter. But we have already stated that interdiction of the mufti, doctor, and transporter is not technical interdiction. It is stated in Radd al-Muhtar: As for interdiction of the mischievous mufti and his like, it is not technical interdiction. This applies if he reached adulthood as a mature intelligent person and then became foolish. But if he reached adulthood as foolish, the author has explained its ruling by saying: 'If he reaches adulthood' etc. Then after both agree that interdiction is due to foolishness, they differed on whether it occurs simply by foolishness or by a judge's ruling. According to Abu Yusuf, he does not become interdicted except by a judge's ruling, and he does not become free except by the judge's release. According to Muhammad, he becomes interdicted without the judge's ruling, and becomes free by abandoning foolishness. It is stated in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others: The fatwa is according to their view (the two disciples). The fool according to them is like a minor in all rulings except in marriage, divorce, manumission, istilad, tadbir, obligation of zakat, hajj, acts of worship, removal of authority of his father and grandfather, the validity of his confession regarding punishments, in awqaf, and in the validity of his bequests for charitable purposes up to one third. In these he is like a sane person. (From al-Ayni, al-Fath, Radd al-Muhtar, and others)
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the rulings of legal interdiction (hajr). It begins by stating that the guardian may authorize or annul the contract of an interdicted person. If interdicted persons cause damage, they are liable for compensation. The confession of a minor and an insane person is not valid in any matter—whether property, hadd punishments, divorce, or manumission—due to the hadith: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the minor until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he recovers,' and because they lack legal capacity. However, a slave's confession is valid regarding his own person but not regarding his master, because the slave has some capacity but his master's rights are protected. The text clarifies a grammatical issue regarding the pronoun used for the categories of persons. It then distinguishes between two types of insane: the maghlub (severely insane) whose actions are completely invalid, and the ghayr maghlub (imbecile) whose actions may be valid. The commentary then explains that if a slave confesses to a property debt, it becomes binding only after manumission, because it is a confession against the master. But if he confesses to a hadd or qisas, it is binding immediately because he is considered free in those matters. The text also addresses the issue of interdiction due to foolishness (safah). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a free, sane adult is not interdicted due to foolishness, because he is a responsible person (mukallaf) and can still destroy his property through permissible means like marriage and divorce, so interdiction would not prevent harm. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that just as a minor is interdicted due to possibility of waste, a confirmed wasteful person should be interdicted in financial transactions, but not in personal matters like divorce or marriage. Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad interdict the fool in all matters. The Hanafi position is that the fool is like a minor only in financial transactions but retains full capacity in personal and ritual matters. The fatwa is according to the Sahibayn, with the condition that interdiction requires a judge's ruling (according to Abu Yusuf) or occurs automatically (according to Muhammad, but fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view).

Key Terms
الحجر (al-hajr): Legal interdiction; a judicial or legal restriction on a person's capacity to act in property matters due to minority, insanity, or foolishness.
المجنون المغلوب (al-majnun al-maghlub): The severely insane person whose intellect is completely disoriented, rendering his actions and statements legally invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Does a slave's confession of a debt bind his master in the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because the master is responsible for the slave's debts.
B) No, because the slave's confession is only binding on himself, and the master's property is protected.
C) Yes, but only if the master gives permission.
D) No, because the slave has no legal capacity.

Key Takeaway
The confession of a minor or insane person is never effective; a slave's confession is valid only for himself.

Interdiction Due to Foolishness (Safah): The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interdiction due to safah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on interdiction due to foolishness and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa does not interdict a fool; the Sahibayn interdict in financial transactions; the fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

This lesson delves into the debated issue of whether a free, sane adult can be interdicted due to foolishness (safah). The Hanafi school has internal disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such a person retains full capacity, while his two disciples limit interdiction to financial matters. Other schools interdict in all matters. The practical consequences are significant for transactions like sale, gift, divorce, and marriage.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions on safah
Abu Hanifa: no interdiction. Sahibayn: interdiction in financial transactions only. Other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali): interdiction in all matters.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is Sahibayn's position.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the safih is a responsible person (mukallaf) and interdiction cannot prevent all harm, as he can still waste through marriage and divorce.
He also uses the principle that a mukallaf cannot be interdicted unless he is prone to fraud.
3
Examine Sahibayn's proof
Sahibayn use qiyas on the minor: if a minor is interdicted due to possibility of waste, then a confirmed wastrel should be interdicted a fortiori.
They distinguish financial transactions from personal status matters.
4
Consider the tarjih
The later authorities (al-Durr al-Mukhtar, etc.) give fatwa on Sahibayn's view, making it the operative position.
The safih is thus treated like a minor in financial matters but not in marriage, divorce, etc.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: According to Sahibayn, a safih's sale without guardian's permission is invalid; his divorce is valid. According to Abu Hanifa, all his transactions are valid.
This affects real-life cases of financial mismanagement.

الحجر وحكمه
يجيزه الولي أو يفسخه، وإن أتلفوا شيئا ضمنوا، ولا ينفذ إقرار الصبي والمجنون، إن شاء أي العقد أي هؤلاء من نفس أو مال وينفذ إقرار العبد في حقه لا في حق سيّده، ويصح إتيان ضمير الجمع، لكن لا يصح الحكم بتوقف العقد، وخيار الولي بالإجازة أو الفسخ مطلقا فإن تصرف المجنون المغلوب لا يصح أصلا، وإن كان راجعا إلى الصغير والرقيق يصح الحكم بالتوقف والخيار لكن ليس إتيان ضمير الجمع على محله، بل كان ينبغي أن يقول: "منهما"، وإن كان راجعا إلى الصغير والرقيق والمعتوه صح الحكم وصح إتيان الضمير، لكن يلزم أن لا يكون بعض المرجع مذكورا. والجواب عنه أنا نختار الشق الثالث ونقول: المجنون على نوعين: مجنون مغلوب وهو الذي اختلط عقله بحيث يمنع جريان الأفعال والأقوال على نهج العقل إلا نادرا وتصرفه لا يصح، ومجنون غير مغلوب وهو الذي يختلط كلامه فيشبه مرة كلام العقلاء ومرة لا وهو المعتوه، ولما ذكر المجنون المغلوب فهم منه غير المغلوب الذي بمنزلة الصبي والعبد فيكون مرجع الضمير مذكورا ضمنا فلا إشكال، ويمكن الجواب باختيار الشق الثاني ونقول: أتي بضمير الجمع وأراد به التثنية وهو شائع كذا قيل هذا ملخص ما في التكملة و"ملا مسكين"، وفيه كلام طويل ليس هذا موضعه.
ضمنوا؛ لما وإن أتلفوا شيئا إلخ: هذا تفريع على قوله: "لا" فعلا": أي إن أتلف هؤلاء المحجورون شيئا من نفس أو مال أنه لا حجر في أفعال الجوارح؛ لأن اعتبار الفعل لا يتوقف على القصد، فإن النائم إذا انقلب على مال إنسان وأتلفه، ضمن، وإن عدم القصد، لكنه لا يخاطب بالأداء إلا عند القدرة كالمعسر لا يطالب بالدين إلا إذا أيسر، وكالنائم لا يطالب بالأداء إلا إذا استيقظ، وقد اختلفوا في أن الضمان يجب للحال، أو بعد البلوغ والعتق، وظاهر هذا التعليل أنه لا يجب إلا بعد البلوغ والعتق وقد نقل في "التكملة" [١٥٧/٨]: عن "الحدادي"، و"العناية" كلاما يدل على أنه يجب في الحال، ومن أراد التفصيل فلينظر في "التكملة" و"الفتح".
ولا ينفذ إقرار إلخ أي لا ينفذ إقرار الصبي والمجنون مطلقا لا بمال ولا بحد من الحدود ولا بالطلاق ولا بالعتاق؛ لقوله عليه: رفع القلم عن ثلاثة عن الصبي حتى يحتلم، وعن المجنون حتى يفيق، وظاهره يقتضي أن لا يتعلق بأقوالهما حكم [ رمز الحقائق: ۳۱۳/۲]؛ ولأن اعتبار الأقوال في الشرع منوطة بالأهلية، وهي معدومة فيهما، حتى لو تعلق بإقرارهما حكم شرعي كالحد لا يعتبر أيضا إلا من حيث إنه إتلاف، فيجب الضمان، لا يقال: هذا الحكم أي عدم نفوذ إقرارهما علم من قوله: "قولا"؛ لأنا نقول: إنما علم منه بطريق التضمين، والتصريح أبلغ. فكذا ذكره تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥٧/٨]
وينفذ إقرار إلخ: أي ينفذ إقرار العبد في حقه لقيام الأهلية لا في حق سيده رعاية لجانبه؛ لأن نفاذه لا يعرى عن تعلق الدين برقبته وكسبه وكلاهما إتلاف ماله. (فتح)

كتاب الحجر
٢٣٤
الحجر وحكمه
فلو أقرّ بمال لزمه بعد الحرية، ولو أقر بحد أو قود، لزمه في الحال لا بسفه، على نفسه لزوال المانع أي العبد قصاص فلو أقر بمال إلخ: أي لو أقر العبد بمال لأحد لزمه المال بعد العتق لا في الحال؛ لأنه إقرار على غيره، وهو المولى، لما أنه وما في يده ملكه، وإقرار الرجل على غيره لا يقبل، فإذا أعتق زال المانع ووجب المال لوجود الأهلية. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٥٧/٨، ١٠٨] لزمه في الحال أي يلزمه الحد والقود في الحال؛ لأنه يبقى على أصل الحرية في حقهما. تكملة البحر الرائق: ١۵٨/۸] فإن قيل: قال: "لا يملك العبد والمكاتب شيئا إلا الطلاق"، و"شيئا" نكرة في سياق النفي فتعم فيقتضي أن لا يملك الإقرار بالحدود والقصاص؟ قلنا: لما بقي على أصل الحرية في حقهما يكون إقراره بهما إقرار بالحرية لا بالعبدية؛ ولأن قوله تعالى: بَلِ الْإِنْسَانُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بَصِيرَةٌ (القيامة: ١٤) يقتضي أن يصح إقراره ره فينفذ، ولا يقال: إنه خص منه الإقرار بالمال؛ لأنا نقول: الإقرار بالمال ليس بإقرار على نفسه وإنما هو إقرار على غيره فلم يتناوله النص. (فتح، تكملة)
لا بسفه: أي لا يحجر على الحر العاقل البالغ بسبب سفه عند الإمام، والسفه: هو العمل بخلاف موجب الشرع واتباع الهوى ومن عادة السفيه التبذير والإسراف في النفقة والتصرفات لا لغرض أو لغرض لا يعده العقلاء من أهل الديانة غرضا مثل دفع المال إلى المغني واللعاب، وشراء الحمام للطيارة بثمن غال والغبن في التجارات من غير محمدة رمز الحقائق: ۳۱۳/۲] وأصل المسامحات في التصرفات والبر والإحسان مشروع إلا أن الإسراف حرام كالإسراف في الطعام والشراب، قال تعالى: ﴿إِذَا أَنْفَقُوا لَمْ يُسْرِفُوا وَلَمْ يَقْتُرُوا (الفرقان:٦٧)، وعندهما: يحجر السفه في تصرفات لا تصح مع الهزل كالبيع والهبة والإجارة والصدقة ولا يحجر عليه في غيرها كالطلاق والعتاق والنكاح وغيرها، وقال الشافعي: يحجر عليه في الكل لهما: أن الحجر على الصبي لاحتمال التبذير، فلأن يحجر على السفيه مع تيقن التبذير كان أحرى وبه قال مالك وأحمد وله أنه مخاطب فلا يحجر عليه كالرشيد، ولأنه لا يندفع الضرر عنه بالحجر، فإنه يقدر على إتلاف ماله بتزويج الأربع، وتطليقهن قبل الدخول وبعده في كل يوم ووقت، ولو كان في الحجر عليه دفع الضرر جاز كالمفتي الماجن والطبيب الجاهل والمكاري المفلس، لكن قدمنا أن الحجر على المفتي والطبيب والمكاري ليس بحجر اصطلاحي.
قال في "رد المحتار": وأما الحجر على المفتي الماجن وأخويه، فليس بحجر اصطلاحي، وهذا إذا بلغ عاقلا رشيدا ثم سفه، وأما إذا بلغ سفيها، فقد بين المصنف حكمه بقوله: "فإن بلغ إلخ، ثم بعد اتفاقهما على أن الحجر يكون بالسفه اختلفا في أنه هل يكون بمجرد السفه أم بقضاء القاضي؟ فعند أبي يوسف لا يصير محجورا إلا بالقضاء، ولا يصير مطلقا إلا بإطلاق القاضي، وعند محمد يحجر بدون حجر القاضي، وينطلق بترك السفه، قال في "الدر المختار" وغيره: الفتوى على قولهما، ويكون السفيه عندهما كالصغير في جميع الأحكام إلا في النكاح والطلاق والعتاق والاستيلاد والتدبير ووجوب الزكاة والحج والعبادات وزوال ولاية أبيه وجده، وفي صحة إقراره بالعقوبات، وفي الإيقاف وفي صحة وصاياه بالقرب من الثلث، فهو في هذه كالعاقل من العيني والفتح ورد المحتار وغيرها)
The chapter of interdiction and its ruling. The guardian may authorize or annul it. If they damage something, they are liable. The confession of a minor and an insane person is not executed. If he wishes, meaning the contract, meaning these persons regarding life or property. The confession of a slave is executed regarding himself, not regarding his master. The use of the plural pronoun is correct, but the ruling of suspending the contract is not correct, and the guardian has the option of authorization or annulment absolutely. Indeed, the action of the severely insane (maghlub) is not valid at all. But if it refers to the minor and the slave, the ruling of suspension and option is correct, but the use of the plural pronoun is not in its proper place; rather it should say 'from them both' (minhuma). And if it refers to the minor, the slave, and the imbecile (ma'tuh), the ruling is correct and the use of the pronoun is correct, but it would require that some referent is not mentioned. The response is that we choose the third option and say: the insane are of two types: the severely insane whose intellect is so confused that it prevents actions and words from following a rational pattern except rarely, and his actions are not valid; and the non-severely insane whose speech is mixed, sometimes resembling rational speech and sometimes not, and he is the imbecile. Since the severely insane was mentioned, the non-severely insane is understood, who is like the minor and slave, so the referent of the pronoun is implicitly mentioned, so no problem. It is also possible to choose the second option and say: the plural pronoun was used intending the dual, which is common. This is the summary of what is in al-Takmila and Mulla Miskin, but there is lengthy discussion not appropriate here. They are liable; as for 'if they damage something' etc.: this is a branch of his statement 'No' in deed: i.e., if these interdicted persons damage something regarding life or property, there is no interdiction regarding actions of the limbs, because the consideration of the action does not depend on intention. For if a sleeping person rolls onto someone's property and damages it, he is liable despite lacking intention, but he is not addressed for payment until he is able, like the insolvent debtor who is not demanded until he becomes wealthy, and like the sleeping person who is not demanded until he wakes. They differed on whether liability is immediate or after puberty and manumission. The apparent meaning of this reasoning is that it is not due until after puberty and manumission. It was narrated in al-Takmila from al-Haddad and al-Inaya that it is due immediately. Whoever wants details should look into al-Takmila and al-Fath. 'The confession of a minor and an insane person is not executed' etc.: i.e., the confession of a minor and an insane person is absolutely not executed, neither regarding property nor regarding a prescribed punishment nor regarding divorce nor regarding manumission, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'The pen is lifted from three: from the minor until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he recovers.' Its apparent meaning requires that no ruling is attached to their statements. And because the consideration of statements in the Sharia is dependent on legal capacity, which is absent in both. Even if a legal ruling like a prescribed punishment is attached to their confession, it is not considered except from the aspect that it is destruction, so liability is required. It cannot be said: this ruling, i.e., the non-execution of their confession, is known from his statement 'statement' (qawlan); because we say: it is only known from it by implication, and explicit statement is more emphatic. This is mentioned in Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. 'The confession of a slave is executed' etc.: i.e., the confession of a slave is executed regarding himself due to the existence of legal capacity, not regarding his master, out of consideration for the master's side, because its execution is not free from entailing debt on his person and his earnings, both of which are destruction of his property. (Al-Fath) Now i.e., the [PAGE_235] Chapter of Interdiction 234. The chapter of interdiction and its ruling. If he confesses to a property, it becomes binding after manumission. If he confesses to a prescribed punishment or retaliation, it becomes binding immediately. Not due to foolishness, on himself due to the removal of the barrier, i.e., the slave. Retaliation. 'If he confesses to property' etc.: i.e., if a slave confesses to a property for someone, the property becomes binding after manumission, not immediately, because it is a confession against another, i.e., the master, since what he possesses belongs to his master. The confession of a person against another is not accepted. When he is freed, the barrier is removed and the property becomes due due to the existence of legal capacity. Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. 'Immediately' i.e., the prescribed punishment and retaliation become binding immediately because he remains on the original freedom regarding them. Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. If it is said: He (the Prophet) said: 'The slave and the mukatib do not own anything except divorce,' and 'anything' is indefinite in the context of negation so it generalizes, implying that he does not own confession regarding punishments and retaliation? We reply: Since he remains on the original freedom regarding them, his confession regarding them is a confession of freedom, not of slavery. And because the statement of Allah: 'Rather, man is a witness against himself' (Qiyamah: 14) implies that his confession is valid and executed. And it cannot be said that confession regarding property is excepted from that; because we say: confession regarding property is not a confession against himself but rather against another, so the text does not cover it. (Al-Fath, Takmila) 'Not due to foolishness' (la bisafah): i.e., a free, sane, adult person is not interdicted due to foolishness according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). Foolishness (safah) is acting contrary to the requirements of the Sharia and following whims. It is the habit of the fool (safih) to waste and overspend in expenses and transactions for no purpose or for a purpose that rational people of religion do not consider a purpose, such as giving money to a singer or a player, buying pigeons for flying at an exorbitant price, and being cheated in trades without commendation. The basic principle of leniency in transactions and charity and beneficence is legislated, but extravagance is forbidden, like extravagance in food and drink. Allah said: 'When they spend, they are not extravagant and not miserly' (Al-Furqan: 67). According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the fool is interdicted in transactions that are not valid with jest, like sale, gift, lease, and charity, but he is not interdicted in others like divorce, manumission, marriage, and others. Al-Shafi'i said: He is interdicted in all. For them (the two disciples): Interdiction of a minor is due to the possibility of waste, so it is more appropriate to interdict the fool with confirmed waste. Malik and Ahmad also said this. For him (Abu Hanifa): He is legally addressed, so he is not interdicted, like the mature person. And because harm cannot be repelled from him by interdiction, for he is able to destroy his property by marrying four women and divorcing them before and after consummation every day and time. If interdiction repelled harm, it would be permissible, like the mischievous mufti, the ignorant doctor, and the bankrupt transporter. But we have already stated that interdiction of the mufti, doctor, and transporter is not technical interdiction. It is stated in Radd al-Muhtar: As for interdiction of the mischievous mufti and his like, it is not technical interdiction. This applies if he reached adulthood as a mature intelligent person and then became foolish. But if he reached adulthood as foolish, the author has explained its ruling by saying: 'If he reaches adulthood' etc. Then after both agree that interdiction is due to foolishness, they differed on whether it occurs simply by foolishness or by a judge's ruling. According to Abu Yusuf, he does not become interdicted except by a judge's ruling, and he does not become free except by the judge's release. According to Muhammad, he becomes interdicted without the judge's ruling, and becomes free by abandoning foolishness. It is stated in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others: The fatwa is according to their view (the two disciples). The fool according to them is like a minor in all rulings except in marriage, divorce, manumission, istilad, tadbir, obligation of zakat, hajj, acts of worship, removal of authority of his father and grandfather, the validity of his confession regarding punishments, in awqaf, and in the validity of his bequests for charitable purposes up to one third. In these he is like a sane person. (From al-Ayni, al-Fath, Radd al-Muhtar, and others)
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the rulings of legal interdiction (hajr). It begins by stating that the guardian may authorize or annul the contract of an interdicted person. If interdicted persons cause damage, they are liable for compensation. The confession of a minor and an insane person is not valid in any matter—whether property, hadd punishments, divorce, or manumission—due to the hadith: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the minor until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he recovers,' and because they lack legal capacity. However, a slave's confession is valid regarding his own person but not regarding his master, because the slave has some capacity but his master's rights are protected. The text clarifies a grammatical issue regarding the pronoun used for the categories of persons. It then distinguishes between two types of insane: the maghlub (severely insane) whose actions are completely invalid, and the ghayr maghlub (imbecile) whose actions may be valid. The commentary then explains that if a slave confesses to a property debt, it becomes binding only after manumission, because it is a confession against the master. But if he confesses to a hadd or qisas, it is binding immediately because he is considered free in those matters. The text also addresses the issue of interdiction due to foolishness (safah). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a free, sane adult is not interdicted due to foolishness, because he is a responsible person (mukallaf) and can still destroy his property through permissible means like marriage and divorce, so interdiction would not prevent harm. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that just as a minor is interdicted due to possibility of waste, a confirmed wasteful person should be interdicted in financial transactions, but not in personal matters like divorce or marriage. Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad interdict the fool in all matters. The Hanafi position is that the fool is like a minor only in financial transactions but retains full capacity in personal and ritual matters. The fatwa is according to the Sahibayn, with the condition that interdiction requires a judge's ruling (according to Abu Yusuf) or occurs automatically (according to Muhammad, but fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view).

Key Terms
السفه (al-safah): Foolishness; acting contrary to Sharia, wasting money, and unreasonable spending. It is grounds for interdiction in financial matters according to Sahibayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi position, in which types of transactions is a fool (safih) interdicted?
A) All transactions, including divorce and manumission
B) Only financial transactions such as sale, gift, and lease
C) Only personal status matters like marriage
D) No transactions; a fool is never interdicted

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that the safih is interdicted only in financial transactions (not in personal matters like marriage or divorce).

Interdiction Due to Debt: Hanafi Internal Dispute
Explains the dispute on interdiction for debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on interdiction for debt and explain the practical difference between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's views.

Core Idea
Debt alone does not justify interdiction; imprisonment suffices — but the Sahibayn permit interdiction, and fatwa follows them.

This passage addresses a key financial dispute within the Hanafi school: should a debtor who refuses to pay be interdicted (i.e., have his legal capacity restricted)? Imam Abu Hanifa strongly opposes interdiction due to debt, considering it an excessive harm to the debtor's dignity. However, his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, permit it to protect creditors' rights. The commentary explains the reasoning behind each view and clarifies that later fatwa relies on the Sahibayn's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the passage discusses whether a debtor can be interdicted due to unpaid debt. Abu Hanifa says no; the Sahibayn say yes (and fatwa is on their view).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with a clear mufta bihi.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa argues interdiction nullifies legal capacity and likens the person to an animal, causing great harm. Instead, the judge may imprison the debtor to compel payment.
Imprisonment is seen as less harmful and sufficient to pressure payment.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn allow interdiction to protect creditors from the debtor dissipating assets. If creditors request, the judge interdicts, sells property, and prevents harmful transactions.
This view is considered stronger for protecting rights.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the debtor retains full legal capacity but may be imprisoned; under the Sahibayn, he is interdicted and his assets are managed by the judge.
This affects the debtor's ability to enter contracts during the period.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa adopts the Sahibayn's view, as stated in Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Thus, in practice, interdiction for debt is permissible.
This is the operative position for Hanafi judges today.

ودين بالجر أيضا عطف على قوله : لا بسفه يعني لا يحجر عليه بسبب دين، وإن طلب غرماؤه الحجر عليه، وهذا عند الإمام؛ لأن في الحجر عليه إهدار أهليته وإلحاقه بالبهائم، وذلك ضرر عظيم، فلا يجوز، وعندهما: يجوز عليه بسبب الدين، وعلى قولهما الفتوى تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٦٤/٨] وإن طلب غرماؤه إلخ: أي إن طلب غرماء المديون حبسه حَبَسه القاضي لبيع ماله في دينه؛ لأن قضاء الدين واجب عليه، والمماطلة ظلم، فيحبسه الحاكم دفعا لظلمه، وإيصالا للحق إلى مستحقه، ولا يكون ذلك إكراها على البيع؛ لأن المقصود من الحبس الحمل على قضاء الدين بأي طريق كان عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : إذا طلب غرماء المفلس الحجر عليه حجر عليه القاضي، وباع ماله إن امتنع من بيعه، وقسم ماله بين الغرماء، ومنعه من تصرف يضر بالغرماء كالإقرار وبيعه بأقل من ثمن المثل. واعلم أن عبارة نسخ الكنز مختلفة هنا ففي جميع النسخ المطبوعة كما في هذه النسخة وفي جميع الشروح مثل " والتكملة" و"ملا"مسكين هكذا: "ودين" وإن طلب غرماؤه وحبس ليبيع ماله في دينه"، فعلى هذا يكون قوله : وإن طلب غرماؤه موصولا بقوله ودين والواو وصلية يعني لا يحجر بسبب دين وإن طلب إلخ، ويقدر في قوله: و"حبس إلخ " بأن طلب غرماء الحبس، وعلى ما في النسخ المطبوعة يكون قوله : "وإن طلب غرماؤه حبسه" شرطا، وقوله: "حبسه جزاء له، ويقدر عند قوله: "ودين" وإن طلب غرماؤه كما قررناه، وإنما أثبت في المتن ما رأيت في النسخ المطبوعة والمآل واحد. بلا أمره إلخ : أي إذا كان دينه وماله دراهم، وكذا لو كان دنانير، قضى القاضي دينه بلا أمره؛ لأن للدائن أن يأخذه بيده إذا ظفر بجنس حقه، فكان القاضي معينا له تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٦٥/٨] أو بالعكس: بأن كان دينه دنانير وله دراهم. (عيني) بيع في دينه إلخ بيع الدنانير في الأول والدراهم في الثاني. ملا مسكين)] وهذا بالإجماع، أما عندهما فظاهر وأما عند أبي حنيفة فاستحسان والقياس أن لا يجوز للقاضي بيعه كالعروض، وجه الاستحسان: أنهما متحدان جنسا في الثمنية والمالية، ولهذا يضم أحدهما إلى الآخر في الزكاة، مختلفان في الصورة حقيقة وحكما، أما حقيقة فظاهر، وأما حكما؛ فلأنه لا يجري بينهما ربا الفضل لاختلافهما، فبالنظر إلى الاتحاد يثبت للقاضي ولاية التصرف، وبالنظر إلى الاختلاف يسلب عن الدائن ولاية الأخذ عملا بالشبهين بخلاف العروض؛ لأن الأغراض تتعلق بصورها وأعيانها، أما النقود فوسائل؛ لأن المقصود منها المالية دون العين، فافترقا. (فتح)
And 'dayn' (debt) in the genitive is also a conjunction to his saying 'not due to foolishness', meaning that a person is not interdicted due to debt, even if his creditors request interdiction. This is according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa); because in interdiction there is a nullification of his legal capacity and likening him to animals, which is a great harm, so it is not permissible. According to the two companions, it is permissible due to debt, and fatwa is according to their view (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/164). 'And if his creditors request...' i.e., if the creditors of the debtor request his imprisonment, the judge imprisons him to sell his property for his debt; because paying the debt is obligatory upon him, and procrastination is oppression, so the judge imprisons him to prevent his oppression and to deliver the right to its owner. This is not coercion to sell; because the purpose of imprisonment is to compel payment of the debt by any means according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions say: if the creditors of the insolvent request interdiction, the judge places him under interdiction and sells his property if he refuses to sell it, and distributes his wealth among the creditors, and prevents him from any transaction that harms the creditors, such as acknowledgment (of debt) or selling for less than market value. Know that the wording of the copies of Kanz differs here; in all printed copies as in this copy and in all commentaries such as al-Takmila and Mulla Muskin, it is: 'And debt, and if his creditors request, and he is imprisoned to sell his property for his debt.' Thus, his saying 'and if his creditors request' is connected to his saying 'debt' with a conjunctive waw, meaning he is not interdicted due to debt even if they request, etc. And in the phrase 'and he is imprisoned' it is estimated as 'if the creditors request imprisonment'. According to the printed copies, his saying 'and if his creditors request his imprisonment' is the condition, and 'he is imprisoned' is the result. The end result is the same. 'Without his order etc.': i.e., if his debt and his property are both dirhams, and likewise if both are dinars, the judge pays his debt without his order; because the creditor may take it himself if he finds the same type as his right, so the judge is assisting him (Takmila 8/165). Or the opposite: his debt is dinars and he has dirhams (or vice versa). ('Ayni) 'is sold for his debt' means: in the first case dinars are sold, in the second dirhams. This is by consensus (ijma'). According to the two companions it is obvious, but according to Abu Hanifa it is istihsan; qiyas would be that it is not permissible for the judge to sell it like other commodities. The basis of istihsan is that they are united in genus (jins) in terms of being currency and monetary value, therefore one is combined with the other in zakat, but they differ in form (surah) in reality and legally. In reality it is obvious; legally, because usury of excess (riba al-fadl) does not occur between them due to their difference. So considering the unity, the judge's authority to act is established; considering the difference, the creditor's authority to take is negated, acting on both resemblances (shabah). Unlike other commodities (urud), because objectives are attached to their forms and specific items; whereas currencies are means, because the purpose is monetary value not the specific coin, so they are different. (Fath)
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage deals with the issue of financial interdiction due to debt. According to Abu Hanifa, a debtor is not interdicted even at the request of creditors, because interdiction strips the person of legal capacity, likening him to an animal, which is excessive harm. Instead, the judge may imprison the debtor to compel payment. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit interdiction of an insolvent debtor, and fatwa is given according to their view. The text clarifies a manuscript variant of Kanz: the phrase 'and debt, and if his creditors request, and he is imprisoned' indicates that debt alone does not cause interdiction, but imprisonment is a separate measure. The passage then discusses the sale of the debtor's property by the judge. If the debtor's asset is of the same currency as the debt (e.g., both dirhams), the judge can directly pay the debt without the debtor's permission, because the creditor can take his right in kind. If the assets are of a different currency (e.g., debt in dinars, assets in dirhams), the judge may sell the assets to convert them. This is by consensus (ijma') according to Abu Hanifa's istihsan: although qiyas would forbid the judge from selling (like other goods), istihsan allows it because gold and silver share the same genus in terms of monetary function and are combined in zakat calculation, despite being different in form. Since they are means of exchange rather than specific goods, the judge has authority to sell. This contrasts with other merchandise (urud), where the object's specific identity matters, so the judge cannot sell without the owner's consent.

Key Terms
الدين (al-dayn): A debt; here specifically a monetary obligation that the debtor has not paid.
الإفلاس (al-iflas): Insolvency; inability to pay debts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, what is the condition for a judge to interdict a debtor?
A) The debtor must be insolvent and creditors must request it.
B) The debtor must be a minor.
C) The debtor must have committed a crime.
D) The judge may interdict without any request.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal ikhtilaf on interdiction for debt, but the operative position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, allowing interdiction to protect creditors.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Sale of Debtor's Assets for Different Currency: Istihsan Over Qiyas
Explains the istihsan rule for selling debtor's currency assets for different-currency debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits a judge to sell a debtor's gold to pay a silver debt (or vice versa) using istihsan, and why this overrides the general qiyas rule.

Core Idea
A judge may sell a debtor's gold to pay a silver debt because both share the same monetary genus, despite differing in form.

This passage extends the judge's authority over a debtor's property. When a debtor's assets are in one currency and the debt in another, qiyas would forbid the judge from selling without the owner's consent, just as with other commodities. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan, allowing the sale because gold and silver are united in their function as currency. The reasoning explains that they are means of exchange, not specific goods, and that they are combined in zakat, which shows their essential unity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The debtor owes a debt in one currency (e.g., dinars) but holds assets in another (e.g., dirhams). The judge needs to sell the assets to pay the debt.
This is a common situation when the debtor's available cash is in a different form.
2
State the qiyas rule
By qiyas with other commodities (urud), the judge cannot sell the assets without the debtor's permission because he does not own them.
The qiyas asl is the rule that a judge cannot sell another's property without consent.
3
Explain the istihsan exception
Istihsan allows the sale because gold and silver share the same genus (jins) in terms of being currency and monetary value. They are combined in zakat, and they are means of exchange, not specific objects.
This is based on the functional unity of currency.
4
Contrast with other goods
For other goods (urud), the specific identity matters, and the creditor cannot take them in lieu of debt without consent. Currencies are different because the purpose is monetary value, not the specific coin.
This distinction prevents the rule from being extended beyond currencies.
5
Confirm consensus
The passage states this istihsan rule is by consensus (ijma') among the Hanafis, even Abu Hanifa agrees despite his general reluctance to allow judge's sale without consent.
Consensus solidifies the ruling.

(عيني) بيع في دينه إلخ بيع الدنانير في الأول والدراهم في الثاني. ملا مسكين)] وهذا بالإجماع، أما عندهما فظاهر وأما عند أبي حنيفة فاستحسان والقياس أن لا يجوز للقاضي بيعه كالعروض، وجه الاستحسان: أنهما متحدان جنسا في الثمنية والمالية، ولهذا يضم أحدهما إلى الآخر في الزكاة، مختلفان في الصورة حقيقة وحكما، أما حقيقة فظاهر، وأما حكما؛ فلأنه لا يجري بينهما ربا الفضل لاختلافهما، فبالنظر إلى الاتحاد يثبت للقاضي ولاية التصرف، وبالنظر إلى الاختلاف يسلب عن الدائن ولاية الأخذ عملا بالشبهين بخلاف العروض؛ لأن الأغراض تتعلق بصورها وأعيانها، أما النقود فوسائل؛ لأن المقصود منها المالية دون العين، فافترقا. What is the basis for the judge's permission to sell a debtor's gold to pay a silver debt without the debtor's order?
A) The judge has general authority over the debtor's property.

Hajr Due to Debt: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hajr for debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on hajr for debt and explain the practical difference between Abu Hanifa's view and the Sahibayn's view.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa forbids interdiction for debt to preserve legal capacity; the Sahibayn allow it, and the fatwa follows them.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether a judge may impose legal interdiction (hajr) on a debtor who refuses to pay. The core issue is the balance between protecting creditors' rights and preserving the debtor's legal capacity. We will explore the rational arguments each side presents and see which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Understand what hajr (legal interdiction) means and that the dispute is whether it can be applied due to debt, not folly or incapacity.
The passage contrasts hajr for debt with hajr for folly (safah).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that hajr is not permitted because it squanders the debtor's legal capacity and likens him to beasts, causing great harm. He argues that imprisonment alone suffices.
His evidence includes the hadith 'Qul la khilaba' (Say: no cheating).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that hajr is permitted to protect creditors. The judge may interdict, sell property, and restrict harmful transactions.
They view that imprisonment and interdiction work together.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The text explicitly states 'wa 'ala qawlihima al-fatwa' (the fatwa is on their view), meaning the Sahibayn's position is the operative ruling.
This is a clear tarjih within the Hanafi school.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the debtor retains full legal capacity and can manage his assets; the judge only sells necessary assets. Under Sahibayn, the debtor is interdicted and the judge controls all transactions.
The practical consequence affects the debtor's ability to incur new debts or make contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحجر
الحجر وحكمه
ودين، وإن طلب غرماؤه حبسه، حبسه؛ ليبيعَ ماله في دينه، فلو ماله ودينه دراهم، شرط
جزاؤه المديون
قضى بلا أمره، ولو دينه دراهم وله دنانير أو بالعكس، بيع في دينه
القاضي
بأخذه أي أمر المديون إجماعاً
أي للمديون
كان
. أن يحجر عليه؛ لأنه كان يخدع في البيع، فأقرهم على ذلك، ولم ينكر عليهم، ولو لم يكن الحجر مشروعا لأنكر عليهم قلنا الحديث دليل لنا؛ لأنه عليها لم يجبهم إلى ذلك، وإنما قال: "قل لا خلابة" ولو كان مشروعا لأجابهم إليه. رمز الحقائق: ٣١٥/٢] ودين بالجر أيضا عطف على قوله : "لا" "بسفه" يعني لا يحجر عليه بسبب دين، وإن طلب غرماؤه الحجر عليه، وهذا عند الإمام؛ لأن في الحجر عليه إهدار أهليته وإلحاقه بالبهائم، وذلك ضرر عظيم، فلا يجوز، وعندهما: يجوز عليه بسبب الدين، وعلى قولهما الفتوى تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٦٤/٨] وإن طلب غرماؤه إلخ: أي إن طلب غرماء المديون حبسه حَبَسه القاضي لبيع ماله في دينه؛ لأن قضاء الدين واجب عليه، والمماطلة ظلم، فيحبسه الحاكم دفعا لظلمه، وإيصالا للحق إلى مستحقه، ولا يكون ذلك إكراها على البيع؛ لأن المقصود من الحبس الحمل على قضاء الدين بأي طريق كان عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : إذا طلب غرماء المفلس الحجر عليه حجر عليه القاضي، وباع ماله
" العيني"
"
إن امتنع من بيعه، وقسم ماله بين الغرماء، ومنعه من تصرف يضر بالغرماء كالإقرار وبيعه بأقل من ثمن المثل. واعلم أن عبارة نسخ الكنز مختلفة هنا ففي جميع النسخ المطبوعة كما في هذه النسخة وفي جميع الشروح مثل " و "التكملة" و"ملا"مسكين هكذا: "ودين" وإن طلب غرماؤه وحبس ليبيع ماله في دينه"، فعلى هذا يكون قوله : وإن طلب غرماؤه موصولا بقوله ودين والواو وصلية يعني لا يحجر بسبب دين وإن طلب إلخ، ويقدر في قوله: و"حبس إلخ " بأن طلب غرماء الحبس، وعلى ما في النسخ المطبوعة يكون قوله : "وإن طلب غرماؤه حبسه" شرطا، وقوله: "حبسه جزاء له، ويقدر عند قوله: "ودين" وإن طلب غرماؤه كما قررناه، وإنما أثبت في المتن ما رأيت في النسخ المطبوعة والمآل واحد.
بلا أمره إلخ : أي إذا كان دينه وماله دراهم، وكذا لو كان دنانير، قضى القاضي دينه بلا أمره؛ لأن للدائن أن يأخذه بيده إذا ظفر بجنس حقه، فكان القاضي معينا له تكملة البحر الرائق: ١٦٥/٨] أو بالعكس: بأن كان دينه دنانير وله دراهم. (عيني) بيع في دينه إلخ بيع الدنانير في الأول والدراهم في الثاني. ملا مسكين)] وهذا بالإجماع، أما عندهما فظاهر وأما عند أبي حنيفة فاستحسان والقياس أن لا يجوز للقاضي بيعه كالعروض، وجه الاستحسان: أنهما متحدان جنسا في الثمنية والمالية، ولهذا يضم أحدهما إلى الآخر في الزكاة، مختلفان في الصورة حقيقة وحكما، أما حقيقة فظاهر، وأما حكما؛ فلأنه لا يجري بينهما ربا الفضل لاختلافهما، فبالنظر إلى الاتحاد يثبت للقاضي ولاية التصرف، وبالنظر إلى الاختلاف يسلب عن الدائن ولاية الأخذ عملا بالشبهين بخلاف العروض؛ لأن الأغراض تتعلق بصورها وأعيانها، أما النقود فوسائل؛ لأن المقصود منها المالية دون العين، فافترقا. (فتح)
Book of Interdiction. Interdiction and its ruling. And due to debt: if his creditors request his imprisonment, he is imprisoned so that he sells his property for his debt. So if his property and his debt are dirhams, the judge pays (the debt) without his order. And if his debt is dirhams and he has dinars, or vice versa, it is sold for his debt. The judge takes it upon himself to order the debtor by consensus. That he be interdicted because he used to cheat in selling, so they (the people) approved that, and he (the Prophet) did not forbid them. And if interdiction were not legislated, he would have forbidden them. We say: the hadith is evidence for us; because the people did not ask him to do that, rather he said: 'Say: no cheating' and if it had been legislated, he would have responded to them. The hidden sense: and 'debt' also in the genitive is a conjunct to his saying 'not due to folly' meaning he is not interdicted due to debt, even if his creditors request interdiction upon him. This is according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) because in interdiction there is squandering of his legal capacity and likening him to beasts, and that is a great harm, so it is not permissible. According to the two (Sahibayn): it is permissible for debt, and the fatwa is on their view. The hidden sense: and if his creditors request his imprisonment, the judge imprisons him so that he sells his property for his debt; because repayment of debt is obligatory on him, and procrastination is injustice, so the judge imprisons him to repel his injustice and to deliver the right to its entitled, and that is not compulsion to sell because the purpose of imprisonment is to pressure for repayment of debt by any means according to Abu Hanifa. And the two said: if the creditors of the bankrupt request interdiction upon him, the judge declares interdiction on him, and sells his property if he refuses to sell it, and divides his property among the creditors, and prevents him from any transaction harmful to the creditors, such as acknowledgment of debt or selling for less than market value. And know that the wording of the copies of al-Kanz differs here: in all printed copies as in this copy and in all commentaries like al-Takmila and Mullā Miskīn: 'And debt, and if his creditors request his imprisonment, he is imprisoned to sell his property for his debt.' Thus his saying 'and if his creditors request' is connected to the word 'debt' and the waw is conjunctive, meaning he is not interdicted due to debt even if they request, etc. And in his saying 'and imprisoned etc.' it is meaningful with the phrase 'if the creditors request imprisonment'. And according to what is in the printed copies, his saying 'and if his creditors request his imprisonment' is a condition, and his saying 'he imprisoned him' is the consequence. And they estimate in his saying 'and debt' that if his creditors request, as we established. And I only reproduced in the text what I saw in the printed copies, and the outcome is one. 'Without his order etc.': meaning if his debt and property are dirhams, and likewise if they were dinars, the judge pays his debt without his order; because the creditor can take it himself if he finds the same type of his right, so the judge is assisting him. Or vice versa: that his debt is dinars and he has dirhams. The sale is for his debt: the dinars are sold in the first case and the dirhams in the second. And this is by consensus. According to the two it is apparent, and according to Abu Hanifa it is istihsan, and the qiyas is that the judge may not sell them like goods. The reason for istihsan: they are unified in genus regarding currency and value, therefore one is added to the other in zakah, and they differ in form actually and legally. Actually it is apparent, legally because riba al-fadl does not occur between them due to their difference. So considering the unity, the judge has the power to dispose, and considering the difference, the creditor's right to take is negated, acting on both aspects. This is contrary to goods because purposes are attached to their forms and entities, whereas coins are means because the intention is their value not their entity, so they differ.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding legal interdiction (hajr) due to debt. The passage opens by stating the ruling: if creditors request the debtor's imprisonment, the judge may imprison him to force the sale of his assets. However, the core issue is whether the judge can impose interdiction (restriction on legal capacity) due to debt. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that interdiction for debt is not permitted because it effectively nullifies the debtor's legal capacity and likens him to a beast, which is a severe harm. Instead, the debtor is imprisoned to pressure him to pay, but his legal capacity remains intact. The Sahibayn argue that interdiction is permissible for debt; the judge may declare the debtor interdicted, sell his property, divide the proceeds among creditors, and restrict his harmful transactions. The fatwa (mufta bihi) is given on the view of the Sahibayn. The passage then discusses the procedure when the debtor has cash (dirhams or dinars). If the debtor's property and debt are both dirhams (or both dinars), the judge may pay the debt directly from the property without the debtor's order, by consensus. If the debt is one currency and the property is another, the judge sells the property to pay the debt. This is also by consensus but based on istihsan for Abu Hanifa; the qiyas would be that the judge cannot sell coins as they are like goods. The reason for istihsan is that coins are unified in their function as currency and value, unlike goods whose purposes are tied to their specific forms.

Key Terms
الحجر (al-hajr): Legal interdiction; restricting a person's financial capacity due to incapacity or indebtedness.
الإفلاس (al-iflas): Insolvency; a legal status declared when a debtor's debts exceed his assets.
الغرما (al-ghurma'): Creditors; plural of gharim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view regarding legal interdiction (hajr) due to debt?
A) Hajr is not permitted under any circumstances.
B) Hajr is permitted, and the fatwa is on the view of the Sahibayn.
C) Hajr is permitted only if the debtor has no assets.
D) Hajr is permitted only for non-Muslim debtors.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa permits interdiction for debt, but Abu Hanifa's alternative view preserves the debtor's legal capacity through imprisonment alone.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
Judge's Authority to Sell Debtor's Assets: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on judge's sale of debtor's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the judge's sale of a debtor's goods and real estate, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The judge may sell the debtor's goods and real estate per the Sahibayn; this is the fatwa.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a judge can sell a debtor's movable and immovable property to satisfy a debt. While Imam Abu Hanifa held that the judge could only imprison the debtor, his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, allowed the sale. The commentary explains the order of sale and humane exceptions, and concludes that the fatwa follows the Sahibayn's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing positions
Read the opening lines to find Abu Hanifa's view (judge does not sell, only imprisons) and the Sahibayn's view (judge may sell).
Look for the phrases 'ولم يبع عرضه وعقاره' and 'وقالا: يبيع القاضي'.
2
Understand the reasoning behind each position
Abu Hanifa restricts the judge's power to avoid forcing a sale; the Sahibayn view the judge as a supervisor who must balance interests.
The text does not elaborate but implies these rationales.
3
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text explicitly states 'wa al-fatwa 'ala qawl al-Sahibayn' (the fatwa is on the saying of the two companions).
This is a clear tarjih.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the debtor keeps his goods indefinitely; under the Sahibayn, the judge can sell them to pay creditors.
This affects creditor recovery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يبع عرضه وعقاره ،وإفلاس، فإن أفلس مبتاع عين،
أي القاضي
مشتري قبضه بالأذن ولم يؤد ثمنه
ولم يبع عرضه إلخ : أي لم يبع القاضي عرض المديون وعقاره في قضاء دينه، ولكن يحبس أبدا حتى يقضي دينه، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة حالته، وقالا : يبيع القاضي على المديون العرض والعقار إن امتنع من البيع بنفسه، لكن يبدأ ببيع النقود، فإن فضل شيء من الدين باع ،العروض، فإن لم يف ثمنها بالدين باع العقار، وقيل: يبدأ القاضي ببيع ما يخشى عليه التوى أي الهلاك من عروضه ثم ما لا يخشى عليه التلف منه، ثم يبيع العقار. فالحاصل أن القاضي نصب ناظرا، فينبغي له أن ينظر للمديون كما ينظر للدائن فيبيع ما كان أنظر له، ويترك دست من ثيابه ويباع الباقي، وقيل: دستان؛ لئلا يقعد خلال بيته ملوما محسورا إذا غسل ثيابه، وكذا المسكن، يترك له مسكن، ويباع الباقي لو كان له مساكن ولو كان له مسكن ويمكنه أن يجتزئ بما دونه يباع، ويقضى ببعض الثمن الدين، ويشترى بالباقي مسكن يكفيه، وهكذا حال الثياب إذا كان له ثياب يلبسها ويجتزئ بما دون ذلك، والفتوى على قول الصاحبين.
.
وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا كان حاضرا، وأما إذا كان غائبا، فلا يملك القاضي بيع عقاره وعرضه؛ لأنه قضاء على الغائب. ولو أقر بمال يلزمه بعد الديون ما لم يكن ثابتا بالبينة أو علم القاضي، فإنه حينئذ يزاحم الغرماء، كما إذا استهلك مالا لأحد، فإنه يزاحم الغرماء، ولو استفاد مالا آخر بعد الحجر، نفذ إقراره فيه؛ لأن حق الغرماء تعلق بالمال الموجود وقت الحجر دون الحادث. وينفق على المحجور المديون، وعلى زوجته وأولاده الصغار وذوي أرحامه . من ماله؛ لأن حاجته الأصلية مقدمة على حق الغرماء. (عيني، فتح، تكملة، ملا مسكين)
And he (the judge) does not sell his goods and his real estate. And insolvency, then if the buyer of a specific thing becomes insolvent... [commentary:] 'And he does not sell his goods and his real estate' etc.: meaning the judge does not sell the goods and real estate of the debtor in repayment of his debt, but imprisons him forever until he pays his debt. This is according to Abu Hanifa in his state. And the two (Sahibayn) said: the judge sells the goods and real estate of the debtor if he refuses to sell himself, but he begins with selling cash; then if anything remains of the debt, he sells the goods; if their price is not enough for the debt, he sells the real estate. And it is said: the judge begins by selling what is feared to perish (i.e., spoil) from his goods, then what is not feared to perish, then sells real estate. So the conclusion is that the judge is appointed as an overseer; he should consider what is best for the debtor as he considers for the creditor, so he sells what is more advantageous for him, and he leaves one set of his clothes and sells the rest. And it is said: two sets, lest he sit in his house blameworthy and destitute when he washes his clothes. Likewise the dwelling: he leaves for him a dwelling, and sells the rest if he has multiple dwellings. And if he has a dwelling and can content himself with a lesser one, it is sold, and part of the price is used to pay the debt, and with the rest a sufficient dwelling is bought. And similarly for clothes if he has clothes he wears and can content himself with less. And the fatwa is on the saying of the two companions (Sahibayn). This difference of opinion is when he (the debtor) is present; but if he is absent, the judge does not have the right to sell his real estate and goods because it is a judgment against an absent person. And if he acknowledges a debt incumbent upon him after debts, as long as it is not proven by evidence or known to the judge, then he competes with the creditors. Similarly, if he consumes someone's property, he competes with the creditors. And if he acquires other property after the interdiction, his acknowledgment is effective regarding it because the creditors' right attaches to the property existing at the time of interdiction, not the newly acquired property. And expenses are spent on the interdicted debtor, his wife, his young children, and his maternal relatives from his property, because his original need is given precedence over the right of the creditors.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on legal interdiction for debt, specifically focusing on the judge's authority to sell the debtor's movable goods ('urud) and real estate ('aqar). The passage begins by stating that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the judge does not sell these assets; instead, the debtor is imprisoned indefinitely until he pays. The Sahibayn, however, allow the judge to sell both goods and real estate if the debtor refuses to sell them himself. The passage then details the order of sale: cash first, then goods, then real estate. There is also a discussion on prioritizing sale of perishable goods. The judge is advised to consider the debtor's interest as well: he must leave the debtor one set of clothing (or two according to some) and a suitable dwelling. This humane consideration ensures the debtor is not left destitute. The fatwa is given on the Sahibayn's view. The passage then adds additional rules: if the debtor is absent, the judge cannot sell his property as it would be a judgment against an absent person. Regarding acknowledgments (iqrar), if the debtor acknowledges a debt after the existing debts, it is effective only for property acquired after interdiction, not for property already attached by creditors. The passage concludes by stating that maintenance (nafaqah) for the debtor, his wife, children, and needy relatives is given priority from his property over the creditors' claims.

Key Terms
العرض (al-'ard): Movable goods other than cash, such as merchandise, livestock, etc.
العقار (al-'aqar): Real estate; immovable property like land and buildings.
دست من ثيابه (dast min thiyabihi): A set of clothes; the minimum clothing necessary for the debtor's decency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (the Sahibayn), what is the first category of assets the judge should sell to satisfy the debt?
A) Real estate (aqar)
B) Movable goods (urud)
C) Cash (nuqud)
D) Perishable goods only

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position of the Sahibayn allows the judge to sell the debtor's goods and real estate, with cash first, and leaving necessities.

Practical Rules for Debt Enforcement: Order, Necessities, and Special Cases
Practical implementation of debt enforcement in Hanafi law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the order of sale a judge must follow, list the necessities that must be left for the debtor, and state the basic rules for absent debtors, acknowledgments, and maintenance.

Core Idea
Judge sells cash first, then goods, then real estate, always leaving sufficient clothing and a dwelling.

Beyond the intra-madhhab dispute, the passage provides detailed guidance for the judge's practical execution. It specifies the order of selling assets, the humane requirement to leave the debtor necessary clothing and a dwelling, and additional rules for special situations like absent debtors, acknowledgments after interdiction, and the priority of maintenance over creditors. These rules ensure a balanced enforcement that respects both the creditor's right and the debtor's dignity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the order of sale
Read the commentary to find the sequence: cash first, then goods (with perishables prioritized), then real estate.
Look for 'يبدأ ببيع النقود' then 'العروض' then 'العقار'.
2
Understand the humane provisions
Note that the judge must leave the debtor one set of clothing (or two) and a dwelling. If the debtor has multiple, the excess is sold.
This prevents destitution.
3
Recognize the rule for absent debtors
If the debtor is absent (gha'ib), the judge cannot sell his property because it is a judgment against an absent person.
This is a procedural safeguard.
4
Note rules on acknowledgments and maintenance
The debtor's acknowledgment after interdiction only affects newly acquired property. Maintenance of the debtor and his dependents is prioritized over creditors.
This protects basic needs.

D) The debtor's clothes

Key Takeaway
The judge must follow a strict order of sale (cash, goods, then real estate) and always leave the debtor basic necessities like clothing and a dwelling.
